This alteration is predicted to lead to a truncated or absent protein, and truncating variants in PALB2 are known to be pathogenic. This variant has been identified in 8/113732 Non-Finnish European chromosomes by the Genome Aggregation Database (gnomAD: http://gnomad.broadinstitute.org ) and has been reported in individuals with breast, ovarian, pancreatic, and colorectal cancers (PubMed 20122277, 20582465, 21285249, 24061862, 20412113, 29478780). Heterozygous germline pathogenic PALB2 variants have been associated with an increased risk of breast cancer (PubMed 25099575 ) and pancreatic cancer (PubMed 19264984 ). Biallelic mutations in PALB2 have been associated with Fanconi anemia, an autosomal recessive condition characterized by physical abnormalities, bone marrow failure, and increased risk of malignancy (https://www.ncbi.nlm.nih.gov/books/NBK1401/). The heterozygous germline mutation, VHL c.598C>T, changes an Arginine to a Tryptophan at amino acid position 200 (p.Arg200Trp). The estimated carrier frequency for this variant is about 1 in 20 in the Chuvash population (PubMed 11987242 ). It is present in 10/16,278 South Asian and 17/65,908 European chromosomes in the ExAC database. This variant has been established to be pathogenic for autosomal recessive Chuvash polycythemia (PubMed 12415268 , 14726398, 12393546, 12844285), which is characterized by increased red blood cell mass, increased serum levels of erythropoietin and normal oxygen affinity. Studies have suggested that VHL p.Arg200Trp heterozygous carriers do not have increased incidence of VHL-related cancers (PubMed 12415268 , 14726398). In summary, based on the previous reports of this variant in individuals with Chuvash polycythemia, this variant meets our criteria to be classified as pathogenic for autosomal recessive Chuvash polycythemia."

The RTEL1 c.3791G>A alteration results in a missense change of Arginine to Histidine at residue 1264 (p.Arg1264His). This variant has been identified in 0.4% of Ashkenazi Jewish chromosomes in gnomAD (http://gnomad.broadinstitute.org/), and has been reported in both homozygous and compound heterozygous states in multiple individuals affected with autosomal recessive Dyskeratosis Congenita (PMID: 24009516, 23453664, 23329068, 23959892).  This variant is considered to be a founder mutation in Ashkenazi Jewish population (PMID: 25047097, 24009516).  In summary, based on the previous reports of this variant in individuals with RTEL1-associated disease, this variant is classified as pathogenic for autosomal recessive Dyskeratosis Congenita.  The RTEL1 gene is associated with autosomal recessive and autosomal dominant dyskeratosis congenita (DC) (23591994, 23453664, 23329068) and autosomal dominant familial pulmonary fibrosis (25848748, 26022962). People with DC are at increased risk for progressive bone marrow failure (BMF), myelodysplastic syndrome (MDS) or acute myelogenous leukemia (AML), solid tumors, and pulmonary fibrosis (20301779)."

APC	324	MSKCC	GRCh37	5	112175211	112175211	+	missense_variant	Missense_Mutation	SNP	T	T	A	rs1801155		P-0015796-T01-IM6									Unknown	GERMLINE				MSK-IMPACT			0	0			ENST00000257430.4:c.3920T>A	p.Ile1307Lys	p.I1307K	ENST00000257430	NM_000038.5	1307	aTa/aAa		"The APC c.3920T>A variant changes an Isoleucine at codon 1307 to a Lysine (p.Ile1307Lys). This variant has been found in 6-10% of the Ashkenazi Jewish population (PMID:9288102 , 23896379.) A large meta analysis found that Ashkenazi Jews carrying the p.Ile1307Lys variant had approximately a 2-fold increased risk of colorectal cancer (OR=2.17, 95% CI=1.65-2.86). However, this same study did not find any increased risk of colorectal cancer among non-Ashkenazi Jews who carry this variant (OR=1.36, 95% CI=0.59-3.13) (PMID: 23576677).
